❓:24. As shown in Figure 3, the diameter A B=14 of the semicircle Gamma, the circle Gamma^{prime} is tangent to A B at point P, and intersects the semicircle Gamma at points Q and R, Q R= 3 sqrt{3}, angle Q P R=60^{circ}, S_{triangle P Q R}=frac{a sqrt{b}}{c}left(a 、 b 、 c in mathbf{Z}_{+}right., (a, c)=1, sqrt{b} is the simplest radical form). Then the value of a+b+c is (quad).(A) 110(B) 114(C) 118(D) 122(E) 126

🔑:Each repainting destroys no more than two borders between cells of different colors.## SolutionEstimate. Let's call a bridge an segment separating two cells of different colors. Initially, we have 98 bridges. Each repainting changes the number of bridges by no more than 2. Therefore, 48 repaintings are not enough.Algorithm. We will repaint all cells from the second to the 98th, then all cells from the third to the 97th, ..., and finally, one 50th cell. After this, the strip will become monochromatic.## AnswerIn 49 repaintings.

Calculating the Radius of the Balls (r): - The circumscribed sphere radius is related to the radius (r) of the ten balls by the equation: [ r(sqrt{6} + 1) = 5sqrt{2} + 5 ] - Solving for (r): [ r = frac{5sqrt{2} + 5}{sqrt{6} + 1} ] - Rationalizing the denominator: [ r = frac{(5sqrt{2} + 5)(sqrt{6} - 1)}{(sqrt{6} + 1)(sqrt{6} - 1)} = frac{(5sqrt{2} + 5)(sqrt{6} - 1)}{5} = (sqrt{2} + 1)(sqrt{6} - 1) ]4. The radius of the sphere in which the pyramid is inscribed is (5sqrt{2} + 5).1. Understanding the Tetrahedron Structure: - The tetrahedron has three layers with 10 balls in total. - Each edge of the tetrahedron has three balls, resulting in an edge length of (4R) (since each gap between adjacent balls is (2R)).2. Circumradius of the Tetrahedron: - The edge length (a) of the tetrahedron formed by the centers of the outermost balls is (4R). - The circumradius (distance from the centroid to a vertex) of a regular tetrahedron with edge length (a) is (frac{sqrt{6}}{4}a). For (a = 4R), this circumradius is (sqrt{6}R).3. Radius of the Enclosing Sphere: - The radius of the enclosing sphere is the distance from the centroid to a vertex plus the radius (R) of the balls: (sqrt{6}R + R = R(sqrt{6} + 1)). - Given the radius of the enclosing sphere is (5sqrt{2} + 5), we solve for (R): [ R(sqrt{6} + 1) = 5sqrt{2} + 5 ] [ R = frac{5sqrt{2} + 5}{sqrt{6} + 1} ] - Rationalizing the denominator: [ R = (sqrt{2} + 1)(sqrt{6} - 1) ]4. Radius of the Inscribed Ball: - The distance from the centroid to the mid-edge balls (which the inscribed ball touches) is (sqrt{2}R). - This distance must equal the sum of the radii of the inscribed ball ((r)) and the surrounding balls ((R)): [ sqrt{2}R = r + R ] [ r = R(sqrt{2} - 1) ] - Substituting (R = (sqrt{2} + 1)(sqrt{6} - 1)): [ r = (sqrt{2} + 1)(sqrt{6} - 1)(sqrt{2} - 1) ] [ r = sqrt{6} - 1 ]Thus, the radius of the inscribed ball is (boxed{sqrt{6} - 1}).]

🔑:# Solution.When ten identical spheres are arranged in this way, the centers A, B, C, D of four of them are located at the vertices of a regular tetrahedron, and the points of contact are located on the edges of this tetrahedron. Therefore, the edge of the tetrahedron is equal to four radii of these spheres, the radius of the outer sphere is greater than the radius of the sphere circumscribed around the tetrahedron by a quarter of the length of the tetrahedron's edge, and the radius of the inner sphere is smaller than the distance from the center of the tetrahedron to its face by the same amount. Consider the section of the tetrahedron by the plane A B M (Fig. 3).![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2024_05_06_424f80418dd801e5b28ag-23.jpg?height=651&width=662&top_left_y=1907&top_left_x=366)Fig. 2![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2024_05_06_424f80418dd801e5b28ag-23.jpg?height=691&width=759&top_left_y=1867&top_left_x=1114)Fig. 3Let the length of the edge of the tetrahedron be a, the radius of the sphere circumscribed around the pyramid of spheres be R, and the radius of the sphere inscribed in the center of the pyramid of spheres be r.In triangle triangle A B M: A M = B M = frac{a sqrt{3}}{2} ; M E = M H = frac{1}{3} A M = frac{a sqrt{3}}{6};A H = B E = frac{2}{3} A M = frac{a sqrt{3}}{3}A E = B H = sqrt{A M^{2} - M E^{2}} = frac{2 a}{sqrt{6}} = frac{a sqrt{6}}{3}.From the similarity of triangles triangle A E M and triangle A H O we have frac{A O}{A M} = frac{A H}{A E} = frac{a sqrt{3}}{a sqrt{6}} = frac{sqrt{2}}{2};A O = B O = frac{sqrt{2}}{2} A M = frac{a sqrt{6}}{4}.In triangle triangle A B O: S_{A B O} = frac{A H cdot B O}{2} = frac{A B cdot F O}{2} Rightarrow F O = frac{A H cdot B O}{A B} = frac{a^{2} sqrt{18}}{12 a} = frac{a sqrt{2}}{4}.Then R = A O + A L = frac{a sqrt{6}}{4} + frac{a}{4} = frac{a(sqrt{6} + 1)}{4} ; and r = F O - F K = frac{a sqrt{2}}{4} - frac{a}{4} = frac{a(sqrt{2} - 1)}{4}.frac{r}{R} = frac{(sqrt{2} - 1)}{(sqrt{6} + 1)} = frac{(sqrt{6} - 1)(sqrt{2} - 1)^{4}}{5} ; r = frac{(sqrt{6} - 1)(sqrt{2} - 1)}{5} R = (sqrt{6} - 1)Answer. (sqrt{6} - 1).## Variant-31

❓:2.34 Let the natural number n have the following property: from 1,2, cdots, n, any 50 different numbers chosen will have at least two numbers whose difference is 7. Find the maximum value of such an n.(China Junior High School Mathematics League, 1987)

🧠:[<think>Okay, let's see. The problem is asking for the maximum natural number n such that if you choose any 50 different numbers from 1 to n, there must be at least two numbers with a difference of 7. Graph Representation: Consider the numbers ( 1, 2, ldots, n ) as vertices in a graph where each vertex ( i ) is connected to ( i + 7 ). This graph is a collection of disjoint paths, each corresponding to a residue class modulo 7.2. Independent Set: An independent set in this graph is a set of numbers with no two differing by 7. The goal is to ensure that the maximum independent set size is 49, so that any 50 numbers must include at least two numbers differing by 7.3. Residue Classes: For each residue ( r ) modulo 7 (i.e., ( 1, 2, ldots, 7 )), the numbers form a path. The length of each path is ( leftlfloor frac{n - r}{7} rightrfloor + 1 ).4. Maximum Independent Set Calculation: The maximum independent set for a path of length ( m ) is ( lceil frac{m}{2} rceil ). Summing this over all 7 residue classes gives the total maximum independent set size.5. Finding ( n ): - For ( n = 7k + t ) where ( 0 leq t leq 6 ), the number of elements in each residue class is ( k + 1 ) for residues ( 1 ) to ( t ) and ( k ) for residues ( t + 1 ) to ( 7 ). - The total maximum independent set size is ( t cdot lceil frac{k + 1}{2} rceil + (7 - t) cdot lceil frac{k}{2} rceil ).6. Key Calculations: - For even ( k ), the total maximum independent set size is ( 7m + t ) where ( k = 2m ). The maximum ( n ) in this case is 90. - For odd ( k ), the total maximum independent set size is ( 7(m + 1) ) where ( k = 2m + 1 ). The maximum ( n ) in this case is 97. - However, further analysis shows that ( n = 98 ) (which is ( 7 times 14 + 0 )) allows a maximum independent set of 49, ensuring any 50 numbers include two differing by 7. For ( n = 99 ), the maximum independent set size becomes 50, which is invalid.Thus, the maximum value of ( n ) is (boxed{98}).,<think>Okay, so I need to find the maximum natural number n such that if you take any 50 different numbers from 1 to n, there must be at least two numbers with a difference of 7. Hmm, this seems like a problem related to the pigeonhole principle. Let me try to figure it out step by step.First, let me understand the problem. We need to ensure that no matter which 50 numbers we pick from 1 up to n, there will always be at least two numbers where one is 7 more than the other. So, we need to structure the numbers from 1 to n in such a way that avoiding a difference of 7 is impossible when selecting 50 numbers. The question is asking for the largest possible n where this condition holds.I remember that the pigeonhole principle often comes into play in problems where you have to guarantee a certain property when selecting a certain number of elements. The idea is that if you have more pigeons than pigeonholes, at least two pigeons must share a hole. Translating that to this problem, perhaps we can divide the numbers from 1 to n into groups (pigeonholes) such that if you pick more numbers than the number of groups, you'll have to pick two numbers from the same group, which would differ by 7. Wait, but here we need a difference of exactly 7, so maybe the groups are designed to have numbers spaced by 7 apart?Let me try constructing such groups. Let's consider numbers modulo 7. Grouping Numbers by Residue Classes Modulo 7: - Numbers from 1 to ( n ) can be divided into 7 residue classes modulo 7: ( 1, 2, ldots, 7 ). - Each residue class forms a sequence where numbers differ by 7. For example, the residue class 1 modulo 7 is ( 1, 8, 15, 22, ldots ).2. Maximizing Numbers Without a Difference of 7: - To avoid having two numbers with a difference of 7, we can pick at most one number from each consecutive pair in each residue class. - For a residue class with ( m ) numbers, the maximum number of numbers we can pick without having two consecutive numbers (which differ by 7) is ( lceil frac{m}{2} rceil ).3. Calculating Maximum ( n ): - We need the sum of ( lceil frac{m_i}{2} rceil ) for all 7 residue classes to be 49. This ensures that picking 50 numbers will exceed this sum, forcing at least one residue class to have two consecutive numbers. - If ( n = 98 ), each residue class has 14 numbers. The maximum number of numbers we can pick from each class is ( lceil frac{14}{2} rceil = 7 ). Summing over all 7 classes gives ( 7 times 7 = 49 ). - If ( n = 99 ), one residue class will have 15 numbers, allowing ( lceil frac{15}{2} rceil = 8 ) numbers, and the other 6 classes will each have 14 numbers, allowing 7 each. The total is ( 8 + 6 times 7 = 50 ), which means we can pick 50 numbers without a difference of 7.Thus, the maximum value of ( n ) such that any 50 numbers chosen will have at least two numbers with a difference of 7 is (boxed{98}).]

🔑:[Solution] Since 50=7 cdot 7+1, by the pigeonhole principle, from the 98 numbers 1,2,3, cdots, 97,98, any 50 numbers chosen must have 8 numbers that have the same remainder when divided by 7. Let the remainder be r, where r in{0,1,2, cdots, 6}.Since 98=14 cdot 7, there are exactly 14 numbers in 1,2,3, cdots, 98 that have a remainder of r when divided by 7. Among these 14 numbers, any 8 different numbers must have two numbers whose difference is 7, meaning 98 has the property mentioned in the problem.On the other hand, in 1,2,3, cdots, 99, we can choose the following 50 numbers.begin{array}{l}1,2,3,4,5,6,7, 15,16,17,18,19,20,21, 29,30,31,32,33,34,35, 43,44,45,46,47,48,49, 57,58,59,60,61,62,63, 71,72,73,74,75,76,77, 85,86,87,88,89,90,91, 99 .end{array}Among these, the difference between any two numbers is not 7, so the 99 numbers 1,2, cdots, 99 do not have the property mentioned in the problem.Therefore, the maximum value of n that satisfies the requirement is 98.

If the constants were also proportional, they would be the same line, but here they are different, so just parallel.Alternatively, since both lines have slope -A/B = -2/3, which is the same. Yep, that works.Alternatively, I could have used another method where the family of lines passing through the intersection of the two given lines is given by combining the equations. Let me try that approach as a check.The family of lines passing through the intersection of 2x - y - 3 = 0 and 4x - 3y - 5 = 0 can be written as:(2x - y - 3) + k(4x - 3y - 5) = 0, where k is a parameter.But since we need a line that is parallel to 2x + 3y + 5 = 0, we can set the slope of the family member equal to the slope of that line.First, let me compute the slope of the family line. Let's expand the family equation:2x - y - 3 + 4k x - 3k y - 5k = 0Combine like terms:(2 + 4k)x + (-1 - 3k)y + (-3 -5k) = 0So, the equation is (2 + 4k)x + (-1 - 3k)y + (-3 -5k) = 0The slope of this line is -A/B = -(2 + 4k)/(-1 - 3k) = (2 + 4k)/(1 + 3k)We need this slope to be equal to -2/3 (from the line 2x + 3y +5=0). So set:(2 + 4k)/(1 + 3k) = -2/3Cross-multiplying:3(2 + 4k) = -2(1 + 3k)Compute both sides:Left: 6 + 12kRight: -2 -6kSet equal:6 + 12k = -2 -6kBring all terms to left:6 + 12k + 2 + 6k = 0 → 8 + 18k = 0 → 18k = -8 → k = -8/18 = -4/9So, k = -4/9. Now, substitute back into the family equation:(2x - y -3) + (-4/9)(4x -3y -5) = 0Let me compute each term:First term: 2x - y -3Second term: (-4/9)(4x -3y -5) = (-16/9)x + (12/9)y + 20/9Combine terms:2x - y -3 -16/9 x + 12/9 y + 20/9 = 0Convert all coefficients to ninths to combine:(18/9 x - 16/9 x) + (-9/9 y + 12/9 y) + (-27/9 +20/9) = 0Compute each part:x terms: (2/9)xy terms: (3/9)y = (1/3)yconstants: (-7/9)So:(2/9)x + (1/3)y -7/9 = 0Multiply all terms by 9 to eliminate denominators:2x + 3y -7 = 0Which is the same equation as before! So that checks out. Therefore, regardless of the method, we get 2x + 3y -7 =0.So, the general equation is 2x + 3y -7 =0. Therefore, the answer should be boxed as boxed{2x + 3y - 7 = 0}Final AnswerThe general equation of the line is boxed{2x + 3y - 7 = 0}.</think>To find the general equation of the line that passes through the intersection point of the lines (2x - y - 3 = 0) and (4x - 3y - 5 = 0), and is parallel to the line (2x + 3y + 5 = 0):1. Find the intersection point of the given lines: - Solve the system of equations: [ begin{cases} 2x - y - 3 = 0 4x - 3y - 5 = 0 end{cases} ] - Substitute (y = 2x - 3) from the first equation into the second equation: [ 4x - 3(2x - 3) - 5 = 0 implies -2x + 4 = 0 implies x = 2 ] - Substitute (x = 2) back into (y = 2x - 3): [ y = 2(2) - 3 = 1 ] - The intersection point is ((2, 1)).2. Determine the slope of the line parallel to (2x + 3y + 5 = 0): - Convert (2x + 3y + 5 = 0) to slope-intercept form: [ 3y = -2x - 5 implies y = -frac{2}{3}x - frac{5}{3} ] - The slope is (-frac{2}{3}).3. Use the point-slope form to find the equation of the line: - Using the point ((2, 1)) and slope (-frac{2}{3}): [ y - 1 = -frac{2}{3}(x - 2) ] - Convert to standard form: [ 3(y - 1) = -2(x - 2) implies 3y - 3 = -2x + 4 implies 2x + 3y - 7 = 0 ]4. Verification using the family of lines method: - The family of lines through the intersection is: [ (2x - y - 3) + k(4x - 3y - 5) = 0 ] - Set the slope equal to (-frac{2}{3}) and solve for (k), leading to the same equation (2x + 3y - 7 = 0).The general equation of the line is (boxed{2x + 3y - 7 = 0}).]

🔑:This problem primarily tests the method for finding the intersection point of two lines and the technique for finding the equation of a line that is parallel to another line.From the problem, we know that the line we are looking for is parallel to the line 2x+3y+5=0. Therefore, we can set the equation of the line we are looking for as 2x+3y+k=0. Next, we find the intersection point of the lines 2x-y-3=0 and 4x-3y-5=0. Solving these two equations simultaneously, we find that the intersection point is (2,1). Substitute the coordinates of the intersection point into the equation 2x+3y+k=0: 4+3+k=0. Solving for k gives k=-7. Therefore, the equation of the line we are looking for is boxed{2x+3y-7=0}.

A circle passes through points ( K ) and ( L ) with its center on the height ( LF ) dropped to the base ( KM ). It is known that ( FM = frac{sqrt{3}}{6} ) and point ( F ) lies on ( KM ). We need to find the area of the circle.1. Coordinates of Points: - Place ( K ) at ( (0, 0) ) and ( M ) at ( left( frac{sqrt{3}}{2}, 0 right) ). - Point ( F ) is located at ( left( frac{sqrt{3}}{3}, 0 right) ) since ( KF = frac{sqrt{3}}{3} ). - Height ( LF ) is calculated using the Pythagorean theorem in triangle ( KFL ): [ LF = sqrt{KL^2 - KF^2} = sqrt{1 - left( frac{sqrt{3}}{3} right)^2} = sqrt{1 - frac{1}{3}} = sqrt{frac{2}{3}} = frac{sqrt{6}}{3} ] - Coordinates of ( L ) are ( left( frac{sqrt{3}}{3}, frac{sqrt{6}}{3} right) ).2. Finding the Center of the Circle: - The center ( O ) lies on ( LF ), so its coordinates are ( left( frac{sqrt{3}}{3}, y right) ). - The distance from ( O ) to ( K ) and ( L ) must be equal: [ sqrt{left( frac{sqrt{3}}{3} right)^2 + y^2} = left| y - frac{sqrt{6}}{3} right| ] - Solving the equation: [ sqrt{frac{1}{3} + y^2} = frac{sqrt{6}}{3} - y ] Squaring both sides: [ frac{1}{3} + y^2 = left( frac{sqrt{6}}{3} - y right)^2 ] Simplifying: [ frac{1}{3} + y^2 = frac{6}{9} - frac{2sqrt{6}}{3}y + y^2 ] [ frac{1}{3} = frac{2}{3} - frac{2sqrt{6}}{3}y ] [ -frac{1}{3} = -frac{2sqrt{6}}{3}y ] [ y = frac{1}{2sqrt{6}} = frac{sqrt{6}}{12} ]3. Radius and Area of the Circle: - The radius ( r ) is the distance from ( O ) to ( K ): [ r = sqrt{left( frac{sqrt{3}}{3} right)^2 + left( frac{sqrt{6}}{12} right)^2} = sqrt{frac{1}{3} + frac{6}{144}} = sqrt{frac{1}{3} + frac{1}{24}} = sqrt{frac{9}{24}} = frac{sqrt{6}}{4} ] - The area of the circle is: [ pi left( frac{sqrt{6}}{4} right)^2 = pi cdot frac{6}{16} = frac{3pi}{8} ]The area of the circle is (boxed{dfrac{3pi}{8}}).]

🔑:Drop a perpendicular OA from the center O of the given circle to the chord KL and consider the right triangles FKL and AOL.## SolutionSince point F lies on the segment KM, thenKF = KM - FM = frac{sqrt{3}}{2} - frac{sqrt{3}}{6} = frac{sqrt{3}}{3}Drop a perpendicular OA from the center O of the given circle with radius R to the chord KL. Then A is the midpoint of KL. Let angle FLK = alpha. From the right triangle FKL, we find that sin alpha = frac{FK}{KL} = frac{sqrt{3}}{3}. Then cos alpha =From the right triangle OAL, we find thatR = OL = frac{AL}{cos alpha} = frac{frac{1}{2}}{sqrt{frac{2}{3}}} = frac{sqrt{3}}{2 sqrt{2}}Therefore, the area of the circle is pi R^2 = frac{3}{8} pi.![](https://cdn.mathpix.com/cropped/2024_05_06_4c124ad32a76c9faf91dg-31.jpg?height=509&width=506&top_left_y=520&top_left_x=776)## Answerfrac{3}{8} pi
